     4.I. Presentation Of The 2024-2025 Rachel Ann Gray Scholarship Winners.

   5. AUDIENCE/PUBLIC COMMENT (NON-AGENDA ITEMS)
       (Any person may address the Board upon any subject within the jurisdiction
       of the Fair Oaks Recreation and Park Distict. Each speaker is limited to a
       maximum of THREE (3) minutes. Any matter requiring Board action will be
       referred to staff or committee for a report and action at a subsequent
       meeting).

   6. CONSENT CALENDAR
       (All matters listed under Consent Calendar are considered by the Board of Directors to
       be routine and will be acted upon in a single motion. There will not be separate
       discussions of these items unless a request is made prior to the time the Board
       considers a motion to approve).

I, Michael J. Aho, District Administrator of the Fair Oaks Recreation and Park District, do
hereby certify that this agenda has been posted at 10326 Fair Oaks Blvd, Fair Oaks, California
and 4150 Temescal Street, Fair Oaks, California at least 72 hours prior to the meeting of the
Board of Directors in accordance with Government Code Section 54950.5, the Ralph M. Brown
Act.

   320 hours (as identified within the table above) which will be compensated at 50% of the employees current hourly rate of pay.
However, upon retirement from the District, a Regular Full-Time employee December choose to utilize their accrued Sick Leave toward
CalPERS service credit with no maximum limit. Employees whose Sick Leave hours exceed 320 hours are noted but the hours in excess
of 320 not calculated as a liability in the table above. A Regular Part-Time employee will be compensated for a maximum of 160 hours
                                    of sick leave at 50% of the employees rate of pay upon termination.

                           REGULAR MEETING

                                Minutes for March 19, 2025

DISCUSSION & ACTION #4:
Discussion and Possible Action Regarding the Bannister Park Boundary Survey and Next Steps
Towards a Potential Disc Golf Course at Bannister Park.
Public Comment Received:
   • Nick Broad, 3934 Bannister Road, Fair Oaks, spoke in opposition to a disc golf course at
       Bannister Park.
   • Brian Branine, 7656 Southcliff Drive, Fair Oaks, spoke in opposition to a disc golf course
       at Bannister Park.
   • Valerie Szathmari, 3910 Bannister Road, Fair Oaks, spoke in opposition to a disc golf
       course at Bannister Park.
   • George Davis, 3901 Bannister Road, Fair Oaks, spoke in opposition to a disc golf course
       at Bannister Park.
   • Alex Bluemel, 7725 Southcliff Drive, Fair Oaks, would like to support a disc golf course
       at Bannister Park but also sees the importance of keeping the natural area of the park
       undisturbed.


DISCUSSION & ACTION #5:
Discussion and Possible Action Regarding Community Request to Return Disc Golf Baskets to
Miller Park Disc Golf Course.
Public Comment Received:
   • Lindsey Kopperund, 4805 Polo Ct, Fair Oaks, spoke in opposition to returning the baskets.
   • Chris Pickard, 4801 Padaro Ct, Fair Oaks, spoke in opposition to returning the baskets.
   • Steven Pugliese, 8057 Sunset Avenue, Fair Oaks, spoke of the risks of the disc golf course
       at Miller Park being brought to the attention of the District.
   • Marissa Pickard, 4801 Padaro Ct, Fair Oaks, said she wished the neighbors of Miller Park
       had had an opportunity to voice their concerns before the course was built like the
       neighbors of Bannister Park are doing.
   • Alex Bluemel, 7725 Southcliff Drive, Fair Oaks, would like to support a disc golf course
       at Bannister Park but also sees the importance of keeping the natural area of the park
       undisturbed.
   • Wendy Tobin of Fair Oaks sent an emailed statement opposing returning the disc golf
       baskets.
   • Jenna Montero of Fair Oaks sent an emailed statement opposing returning the disc golf
       baskets.
   • A public comment form was submitted at the meeting from Kim Hofer, 3930 Bannister
       Road, Fair Oaks, describing the challenges neighbors of Bannister Park have faced in the
       past with people using the park after hours in inappropriate ways.
The Board did not take a vote but provided direction to staff to keep things as they are at Miller
Park with respect to the baskets while staff continues to look for other options for the course.

DISCUSSION & ACTION #6:
Discussion and Possible Action Regarding Adoption of Three Resolutions Directing Preparation
of the Engineers Reports for the Fair Oaks Parks Maintenance and Recreation Improvement

                                               3
           STAFF REPORT

Meeting Date:        April 16, 2025

To:                  Board of Directors

From:                Michael J. Aho – District Administrator

Subject:             Request for Approval of Change Order for Road
                     Paving Around Plaza Park

 I.   Recommendation
      Approve the attached Change Order for $654,046 (Attachment A) for the
      road paving around Plaza Park, necessitated by additional requirements
      from the County Planning Department and other unforeseen circumstances.

II.   Background
      The road paving project around Plaza Park, initially approved under contract
      BP#21-103 with Bob Construction and designed by Cala, has faced a variety
      of unanticipated challenges that have required deviations from the original
      plans:
          • Initial Requirements: The County's original requirement was for
             a 2" grind and overlay for the entire roadway, with the provision to
             close the entire half of the road all the way around the park for
             simultaneous paving, which would have minimized costs and
             expedited completion. Subsequent assessments revealed that a 2"
             grind and overlay is not feasible across various sections of the
             roadway due to insufficient road base and inadequate pavement
             depth. As a result, the work now needs to be completed in sections,
             leading to significant increases in both costs and project duration.
             Moreover, the inability to close the entire half of the road as originally
             planned has complicated logistics and further increased expenses.
          • Revised Execution: Revised Execution: The necessity to
             execute the paving in sections not only extends the duration of the
             project but also substantially increases the costs associated with
             equipment needed to complete the work and with traffic control and
             the use of flaggers. Heavy equipment will be used as efficiently as
             possible, however the length of time that this equipment will be on
              site will be extended due to the segmented approach required by the
              County. Each section requires its own setup and management for
              safety and compliance, adding layers of complexity and cost.
          •   Slope Compliance: Additional modifications have been required to
              meet slope angles that were not specified in the initial bid. These
              new slope requirements, mandated by the County after the bid was
              accepted, have necessitated significant alterations to the planned
              work.
          •   Cost Escalation: The project was initially bid and budgeted based
              on 2022 material costs. However, by the time the revised plans were
              accepted by the County to meet these new requirements, there was
              a considerable increase in material prices and labor, substantially
              raising the overall project costs.

       These combined factors have led to the need for a Change Order to address
       the increased scope of work, the technical challenges encountered with the
       road base, and the financial implications of material cost escalations,
       extended project timelines, and enhanced traffic management needs.

III.   Problem /Situation/ Request
       The County has mandated several changes to the original road paving
       project plans increasing the cost, which include:
          • Implementation of 24-hour flagging and segmented traffic
              control: To ensure safety and maintain traffic flow around the
              construction zones, the County has required 24-hour flagging and
              segmented traffic control measures, adding complexity and cost to
              the project.
          • Compliance with updated slope and drainage requirements:
              Additional engineering and construction efforts are necessary to
              meet new slope and drainage standards not included in the original
              project scope.
          • Modification of the traffic plan to address safety and
              regulatory compliance: Adjustments to the traffic management
              plan are required to ensure safety and compliance with regulatory
              standards, impacting the project timeline and costs.
          • Cost Increase Due to Delay: There has been a significant cost
              increase due to the time lapse between the original bid and the
              acceptance of the revised plans by the County. This delay has
              contributed to escalations in material costs and labor rates, affecting
              the overall project budget.
       Furthermore, in accordance with a Board Directive, all Change Orders
       exceeding $70,000 require approval from the Board of Directors. This
       Change Order, necessitated by the unforeseen requirements and
       subsequent cost adjustments, falls within this category and thus is
       presented for Board review and approval.

IV.    Financial Analysis
       The actual cost of the Change Order without credits is $932,840, reduced
       by credits totaling $262,794, bringing the total cost to $654,046. Below is
       a detailed breakdown of the costs and credits:
              Traffic Control Plans per County Requirements:         $3,500.00
              Traffic Control per County Requirements:               $180,806.00
              Offsite Paving Revised Price per V1-ASI 031.1:         $717,388.69

              Credits Applied:
              Earthwork. Commitment Credit - Offsite Paving Per Contract
              Drawings:                                    $(262,794.00)
              Site Demolition. Commitment Credit - Offsite Demo per Contract
              Drawings:                                    $(8,500.00)
              Execution Requirements. Commitment Credit - Minor Traffic Control
              per Original Plans:                          $(7,500.00)

              Subtotal before Markup:                         $622,900.69
              Bobo Self Perform Markup (15.00%):              $0.00
              Bobo Sub Markup (5.00%):                        $31,145.31

              Grand Total:                                    $654,046.00

       Rescinded Senate Appropriations: The roadwork was initially included
       in the $1.4 million appropriation from Senator Padilla, but these funds were
       rescinded as they were not included in the Continuing Resolution approved
       in March of this year.
       Reapplication for Funds: We are reapplying for these funds for FY 2026
       with the support of Senator Padilla, Senator Schiff, and Representative
       Bera. We hope to have these requests approved again.
       Interim Funding: To manage the increased costs resulting from the
       mandated changes, the District will utilize proceeds from the recent sale of
       the District’s Cell Tower Lease. A total of $654,046 will be transferred into
       the Bond Budget to cover the cost of the road paving Change Order. Should
       the Senate Appropriation funds be re-awarded for this project in the future,
       those funds will be used to reimburse the Cell Tower proceeds, thereby
       preserving the one-time revenue source for other eligible District needs.

Respectfully Submitted,


Michael J. Aho
District Administrator

POTENTIAL CHANGE ORDER TITLE: V1 ASI 31.1 Perimeter Street Work Changes


CHANGE REASON: Design Development


POTENTIAL CHANGE ORDER DESCRIPTION: (The Contract Is Changed As Follows)
V1 ASI 31.1 Perimeter Street Work Changes
Street work changes
- AC Paving
- Limits of work
- Grades
- Concrete Ramp
- Perimeter Curb
- Demo & AB
- AC Paving Cross Sections
- Traffic Control Plan
- Traffic Control Systems

V1 ASI 31.1 - Items related to Bandshell and Playground will be priced in separate PCO.

Per the original set of plans, it was shown that our construction fence would be in the roads and we would be able to shut down the area for
the duration and do our work in sequence. That has since been retracted and the county is requiring roads to either be opened to the public
after hours or be provided with 24-hour flagging to keep traffic moving. Majority of the work involves major grading/cuts so opening the
roads is no feasible so 24-hour flagging is required. This is a massive disruption to the efficiency of this work and also the original price for
all this work was based on 2022 prices and it is now 2025 when this work is being allowed to happen. Bobo attempted to do this work in 2023
but was stopped by the county due to poor design and the need for a full redesign outside of our control.

           STAFF REPORT

Meeting Date:        April 16, 2025

To:                  Board of Directors

From:                Michael J. Aho – District Administrator

Subject:             Approval of a Village Park Construction Project
                     Allowance Increase


I.    Recommendation
      Approve the increase in the Allowance for the contract with Bobo by
      $300,000 to ensure the project can be completed without financial
      interruption. This increased Allowance will be utilized for road paving and
      addressing unforeseen conditions that may be encountered as the project
      progresses. The funding for this increase will be sourced by reallocating
      $100,000 from the Amphitheater Seat Replacement budget surplus and
      $200,000 from the Cell Tower sale proceeds.

II.   Background
      The District's contract with Bobo is approaching its final stages, having
      successfully managed earlier phases that were prone to unpredictability.
      While considerable progress has been made, the project requires additional
      financial resources to address general site issues and unforeseen conditions
      specifically related to road paving. In Bobo’s contract the initial Allowance
      of $1.8 million has been fully allocated due to various unforeseen site
      conditions, weather-related delays, and escalations in material costs. To
      facilitate the completion of the remaining work without disruption, an
      increase in the Allowance is essential. It's important to note that the specific
      funding request for the road paving costs, amounting to $654,046, is being
      addressed under a separate item during this Board meeting.

      Originally, the plan was to fund these additional needs including the Road
      paving through a $1.4 million Senate Appropriation that was awarded for
      FY2025 (through Senator Padilla’s office). However, that federal funding
      was rescinded in March 2025 after the passage of the Full-Year Continuing
       Budget Resolution. In response, the District has reapplied for this funding
       for FY2026, with strong support from Senator Padilla, Senator Schiff, and
       Representative Bera. While we are optimistic about securing those funds
       next fiscal year, the project cannot wait; immediate action is needed to
       cover the shortfall and keep the project on track.

III.   Problem /Situation/ Request
       Allocating this additional $300,000 to the Bobo contract Allowance is being
       requested for the following reasons:
       • Completion of Critical Work: Road paving is a final critical
           component of the project that must be completed to meet project
           specifications and to be able to obtain an Occupancy Permit from
           Sacramento County. Additional change orders are anticipated for the
           overall project as we finalize construction work. Without increasing the
           Allowance, there is a risk that these necessary tasks could exceed the
           current budget, causing delays or requiring urgent action later.
       • Reduced Risk of Overruns: Initially, the project's $1.8 million
           Allowance was completely allocated to manage a variety of unforeseen
           challenges, including unknown underground conditions, delays due to
           adverse weather, product price increases, product availability issues,
           and necessary design changes. The proposed addition of $300,000 to
           the Allowance is specifically designed to address any remaining
           unanticipated issues effectively. This proactive financial strategy is
           intended to mitigate the risk of potential overruns and eliminates the
           necessity for last-minute requests for additional funding from the
           Board.
       • Maintaining Project Momentum: Approving the funding now
           ensures the contractor (Bobo) can proceed with final tasks without
           interruption. This avoids potential contractor
           demobilization/remobilization costs or schedule delays that could occur
           if funding uncertainty forces a slowdown.

IV.    Financial Analysis
       Staff have identified two internal funding sources to cover the $300,000
       Allowance increase without impacting the general fund or requiring new
       external funds:
       • Amphitheater Seat Replacement Project Budget: We propose
           reallocating $100,000 from the Amphitheater Seat Replacement capital
           project to support the increased Allowance. The original budget for this
           project was $906,934, which included an Allowance of $138,035. Given
           the significant progress made on this project, staff is confident that
           $100,000 can be redirected without jeopardizing its completion,
           leaving a balance of $38,035 in the project's Allowance.
       •   Cell Tower Sale Proceeds – Utilize $200,000 from the proceeds of
           the recent cell tower sale. The District currently holds $972,939 from
           this sale in a reserve account. Using $200,000 from this reserve will
           not adversely affect other projects. Importantly, this $200,000 is
           expected to be reimbursed once pending external funds are received:
           the District is awaiting a Prop 68 grant disbursement of $50,005 and
           the release of Federal House FY2022 Appropriation funds (earmarked
           via Rep. Bera’s office) of $560,929. Once these funds are received,
           they will replenish the cell tower proceeds account by the amount used
           for the Bobo contract.

       The combination of these two sources provides the necessary $300,000,
       ensuring the Bobo contract Allowance can be increased now to keep the
       project moving forward.

Respectfully Submitted,


Michael J. Aho
District Administrator
           STAFF REPORT

Meeting Date:        April 16, 2025
To:                  Board of Directors
From:                Michael J. Aho, District Administrator
Subject:             Request for Approval of Proposed FY25/26 Capital
                     Improvement Plan

Prepared By:         Sean Ventura, Parks & Facilities Manager

 I.    Recommendation
       Staff recommends approving the proposed Capital Improvement Plan as
       presented for the upcoming 25/26 fiscal year.

II.    Background
       Staff reviews the Capital Improvement Plan each year in an effort to identify
       changing goals within the District. The proposed Capital Improvement
       Projects will reflect only the upcoming fiscal year with the remainder of
       proposed projects listed for tracking purposes.

       Prior to being presented to the full Board of Directors, the FY25/26 Capital
       Improvement Plan is brought before the Capital Committee for review,
       revision and approval. The committee meeting for the currently proposed
       Capital Improvement Plan was held on April 11th, 2025. Approval of the plan
       was received from the committee at that time.

       Projects proposed for the Capital Improvement Plan are separate to those
       receiving Measure J funding and will typically not utilize resources from the
       general obligation bond.

III.   Problem /Situation/ Request
       It is requested that the proposed FY 25/26 Capital Improvement Plan be
       approved. When proposals are ready to be requested on individual projects
       from the plan, staff will return to the Board of Directors to seek final
       approvals.
IV.    Financial Analysis
       If all proposed projects from the Capital Improvement Plan are commenced
       during the 2025/2026 fiscal year, the total cost to the District would be
       $800,000.

       The following is a breakdown of the potential funding for each of the items:

       In-Lieu Fees
          • Old Library roof and HVAC replacement, minor interior renovations:
              $191,400
          • Preschool floor renovations: $80,000

       Impact Fees
          • District Master Plan update: $150,000
          • Bannister Park Master Plan: $50,000

       General Fund Unreserved Fund Balance
          • District vehicle (carry over from 2024-2025): $60,000
          • Tables for Village facilities (carry over from 2024-2025): $10,000
          • Replacement carnival games: $5,500
          • Christmas decorations for Village Park: $33,000
          • Chair/table replacements – other facilities $54,000
          • Concessions refrigerator: $100,000
          • Amphitheater lobby furniture: $25,000
          • Barrier fencing for events (carry over from 2024-2025): $30,000

       ADA Fund
         • ADA walk path panels: $11,000

       Fund Balances as of March 31, 2025
        Impact Fees:                          $1,807, 567
        In-Lieu Fees:                         $398,867
        Reserve Fund:                         $515,991
        Unreserved Fund Balance:              $1,405,318
        ADA Fund:                             $55,540



Respectfully Submitted,


Michael J. Aho
District Administrator

           STAFF REPORT


Meeting Date:        April 16, 2024

To:                  Board of Directors

From:                Michael J. Aho – District Administrator

Subject:             Addition of an On-Call Theater Tech position to the
                     Salary Schedule

I.     Recommendation
       Staff requests approval to create an on-call Technical Theatre Technician
       position to support events and performances at the Fair Oaks Performing
       Arts Center and other qualified District events. Wages for this position will
       be funded by the individual events in which the technician is scheduled to
       work.

II.    Background
       In 2024, the Board approved the creation of a full-time Technical/Facility
       Supervisor position, which has since been filled. As the planning of
       programming and events at the new Fair Oaks Performing Arts Center
       increase, it has become clear that the workload exceeds what one person
       can manage. Staff recommends establishing a general on-call Technical
       Theatrical Technician role to assist with the technical needs of productions
       and events across District facilities.

III.   Problem /Situation/ Request
       With the opening of the new Fair Oaks Performing Arts Center and the
       continued development of Measure J-funded facilities, the District is
       entering a period of increased programming and operational demand. While
       the Technical/Facility Supervisor provides essential leadership and
       oversight, it has become evident that additional technical support is needed
       to meet the production and event requirements of the facility.

       Staff is requesting approval to formally establish an on-call Technical
       Theatre Technician position. This role will provide crucial support for
       lighting, sound, stage management, and other technical needs on an as-
       needed basis for District events and performances. This flexible, event-
       based staffing model ensures that the District can meet growing demands
       without committing to an additional full-time role at this time.

       This dual approach—introducing an on-call technician role now while
       evaluating a longer-term staffing solution—positions the District to respond
       effectively to immediate needs while planning strategically for future
       growth. (see Attachment A. “Technical Theatre Technician-Job
       Description”)


IV.    Financial Analysis
       Wages for the on-call Technical Theatre Technician position will be funded
       directly through the budgets of the individual events for which the
       technician is scheduled. This means that the position will not have an impact
       on the District’s general fund or require ongoing budget allocation. Instead,
       compensation will be drawn from event-specific revenue sources such as
       ticket sales, rental fees, or program budgets. This pay-per-event structure
       ensures that staffing costs are aligned with event activity and allows the
       District to scale support based on actual programming needs.

Respectfully Submitted,



Michael J. Aho
District Administrator

Attachment A: Job Description
                                              Fair Oaks Recreation & Park District

                                                      Job Description
Job Title:               Technical Theatre Technician
Department:              Arts & Entertainment
Reports to:              Technical Supervisor
FLSA Status:             Non-Exempt
Revised:                 04/01/25
Pay Rate:                Pay range starts at $16.50 per hour

ATTENTION:
Seeking dependable, enthusiastic, and self-motivated Theatre Technicians to support the Fair Oaks Performing Arts Center
(FOPAC) and Fair Oaks Recreation & Park District (FORPD) events. Candidates should have a strong interest or
experience in technical theatre, particularly AV and lighting systems. This on-call/part-time position includes evening and
weekend hours and is ideal for those who thrive in a collaborative, live event environment.

Job Summary: Under the direction of the Technical Supervisor, the Theatre Technician assists with the technical execution
of performances, rehearsals, and community events. Responsibilities focus on operating and maintaining lighting, sound,
and video equipment while also providing general backstage and production support as needed. This role ensures safe and
efficient technical operations while maintaining the high standards of the Arts & Entertainment Division and Fair Oaks
Performing Arts Center.
Hours: Varies depending on event schedules; on-call and part-time, including weekends and evenings.
Essential Functions:
The following duties are typical for this classification. However, incumbents may not perform all of the listed duties and/or may
be required to perform additional or different duties to meet evolving needs:
    • Operate lighting, sound, and projection equipment during events, rehearsals, and rentals.
    • Assist with the setup, strike, and technical load-in/load-out of events and performances.
    • Conduct routine maintenance and basic troubleshooting on AV and lighting equipment.
    • Support technical needs for performers, renters, staff, and community programs.
    • Assist with stage management, backstage safety, and run crew tasks.
    • Communicate effectively and professionally with the Technical Supervisor, event organizers, and fellow staff.
    • Provide support for other District-wide events as needed.
    • Ensure a safe, clean, and organized environment in all technical and backstage areas.
    • Follow all safety procedures and guidelines during technical work.

Job Requirements:
    •   Ability to work independently and as part of a collaborative team.
    •   Maintain a high level of professionalism and customer service.
    •   Ability to lift and carry up to 50 lbs.
    •   Strong organizational, technical, and communication skills.
    •   Familiarity with live event environments and performance spaces.
    •   Comfortable working with ladders, heights, and basic tools and equipment.

Knowledge, Skill and Experience:
Knowledge of various activities and classes that are art inspired or recreational programming for all ages, including facility
and materials, use; techniques, principles, and procedures used to deliver high-quality arts-inspired recreation programs.

    1. Minimum Education required: High school diploma or general education degree (GED); technical theatre
       coursework, hands-on experience, or relevant certification preferred.

    2. Minimum Experience required: One year of experience in AV, stage lighting, or live event production is preferred.
       Experience as a board operator is a plus.

    3. Other requirements: All applicants must be fingerprinted and pass a pre-employment background check. Reliable
       transportation to and from work.

LANGUAGE SKILLS:
Ability to read and interpret technical documents, follow oral/written instructions, and communicate effectively with staff and
clients.

MATHEMATICAL SKILLS:
Basic math skills for measuring cable runs, electrical loads, and calculating simple operations for setup and maintenance.

REASONING ABILITY:
Ability to apply common sense understanding to carry out detailed written or oral instructions. Ability to solve practical
problems and apply sound judgment during high-pressure or time-sensitive situations.

CERTIFICATES, LICENSES, REGISTRATIONS:
Must possess and maintain a valid California class C driver's license, proof of personal vehicle insurance, and a satisfactory
driving record are required. At the option of the appointing authority, persons hired into this class may be required to either
possess at entry or obtain within specified time limits designated licenses, certifications, or specialized education and training
relevant to the area of assignment. CPR/First Aid Certification and/or AV certifications are a plus.

COMPUTER SKILLS:
Basic computer literacy is required. Familiarity with digital lighting consoles (e.g., ETC), QLab, and audio software is desirable.

PHYSICAL AND EMOTIONAL DEMANDS:
The physical demands described here represent those that must be met by an employee to successfully perform the essential
functions of this job. Reasonable accommodations may be made to enable individuals with disabilities to perform essential
functions. The inability to cope with a stressful work environment does not constitute a protected disability.

While performing the duties of this job, the employee is regularly required to sit and frequently required to talk or hear. The
employee is occasionally required to stand; walk; use hands to finger, handle, or feel; reach with hands and arms; climb or
balance; stoop, kneel, crouch, or crawl and talk or hear. Specific vision abilities required by this job include close vision,
distance vision, color vision, peripheral vision, depth perception, and the ability to adjust focus.

Exposed to dust, noise, machinery, moving objects and other vehicles. Performs simple and power grasping, pushing, pulling,
and fine manipulation. May be exposed to constant vibration of equipment for prolonged periods. The position also requires
near and far vision when inspecting and performing work activities, operating vehicles, tools, and equipment, and preparing
paperwork and reports. Performs heavy physical labor, such as lifting (up to 30-50 pounds), carrying heavy objects, and using
a shovel and other equipment to dig. Climbs ladder and works at heights. Exposure to fumes, dust, and air contaminants
which may cause eye and skin irritation. Work involves physical exertion and exposure to bright lighting, loud sounds, and
crowded backstage conditions.

WORK ENVIRONMENT:
The work environment characteristics described here are representative of those an employee encounters while performing
the essential functions of this job. Reasonable accommodations may be made to enable individuals with disabilities to perform
the essential functions. The noise level in the work environment is usually moderate.

Typically works outdoors in varied weather conditions with exposure to sun, heat and inclement weather. Possible exposure
to traffic and other potential hazards. Regularly works inside and maintains District facilities. May be assigned to work
weekends, holidays and irregular hours based on District scheduling needs. May be assigned to work during emergencies,
seasonally-caused circumstances, or special projects and/or events in varying climate and temperature conditions.


HOW TO APPLY FOR THIS POSITION:
When a recruitment opens for this position, an applicant must submit, during the application filing period, an online application
and attach any supplemental information as required in the job announcement, which may include submitting responses to a
supplemental questionnaire. Online resumes and other unsolicited materials may be attached but will not be considered in
lieu of the required online application, unless otherwise specified in the job announcement. FORPD reserves the right to limit
the number of online applications when necessary. Applicants are responsible for maintaining/updating their contact
information through the online application system.

SELECTION PROCEDURES:
Initial Selection Review:
The Fair Oaks Recreation and Park District reviews all initial application materials to identify qualified applicants. Applicants
meeting minimum qualifications will be invited to the first phase of the recruitment process. FORPD reserves the right to refer
only the better qualified applicants if the number of applicants is high. If the number of applicants is high, the review process
may include a secondary screening (by a panel of job knowledge experts) of the applications and/or supplemental
questionnaires in which the better qualified applicants are referred to the next phase of the recruitment process. Because
recruitment processes vary, applicants are advised to thoroughly review the job announcement before submitting their online
application materials.
Testing:
Testing for this position or any other position may include, but is not limited to the following: written exam, practical exam,
panel interview, physical ability test, assessment center, oral presentation, project assignment, etc. If a revision is made to a
testing component during a recruitment process, the assigned recruiter will notify by email all affected applicants.

Americans with Disabilities Act (ADA) Accommodation:
In accordance with the Americans with Disabilities Act, anyone who needs an ADA accommodation for the purposes of
employment testing should contact the assigned recruiter upon opening of a recruitment.
Withdrawing from the Recruitment Process:
Whenever an applicant chooses to withdraw from a recruitment process, he/she is required to submit an email notification to
the assigned recruiter requesting a withdrawal from the process. The email to the recruiter must include the applicant's current
phone number.
Questions:
All questions regarding this position should be directed to the assigned recruiter upon opening of a future recruitment. NOTE:
The provisions of this publication do not constitute an express or implied contract. Any provision in this publication may be
modified or revoked without notice.
Equal Opportunity Employer:
The Fair Oaks Recreation and Park District is an Equal Employment Opportunity Employer.

APPLICATION DEADLINE: Open Until Filled
INTERVIEWS: If selected, interviews will be scheduled through human resources. Candidates must be available to
interview between the hours of 8:00am – 5:00pm, Monday through Friday.

Meeting Date:       April 16, 2025

To:                 Board of Directors

From:               Michael J. Aho - District Administrator

Subject:            Fair Oaks Recreation and Park District (FORPD)
                    Submission to the 2024 State Controller’s
                    Government Compensation in California Report

Prepared By:        Jennifer Larkin, Administrative Services Manager


I.    Recommendation
      Receive and file the FORPD submission to the Government Compensation
      in California (GCC) Report of the California State Controller’s Office (SCO)
      for the 2024 calendar year.

II.   Background
      The SCO uses its independent authority to guard taxpayer dollars, fight
      waste and uncover fiscal fraud and abuse. This report is mandated by the
      order of the State Controller.

      In 2010, the SCO created the GCC website to enhance government
      transparency and provide a single statewide database that is accessible by
      anyone at any time. At first, the SCO collected government compensation
      data as a component of the financial transaction reports from cities,
      counties, and special districts under the authority of Government Code
      sections 53891 and 53892. In 2015, the Legislature explicitly authorized
      SCO to collect compensation data. The SCO is required to publish the
      information on its website under the authority of Government Code section
      12463.

      The GCC website contains pay and benefit information for positions in cities,
      counties, special districts, and state government, including California State
      University (CSU). Other public employers submit pay and benefit
       information on a voluntary basis for positions in superior courts, the
       University of California, community college districts, K-12 education
       providers, First 5 commissions, and fairs and expositions.

       The attached report contains compensation information for all employees
       who worked for the District in 2024, including wages, retirement
       contributions and group insurance contributions.

IV.    Financial Analysis
       There is no financial impact associated with the staff recommendation.


Respectfully Submitted,



Michael J. Aho
District Administrator

03/19/2025

Fair Oaks Recreation Foundation
Board of Directors
Fair Oaks Recreation & Park District

Subject: Request for Financial Assistance – Shakespeare in the Park Stage Rental

Dear Foundation Board of Directors,

I am reaching out to request ﬁnancial assistance from the Fair Oaks Recreation Foundation
to support an upcoming Shakespeare in the Park performance by Take Note Troupe. As you
know, this talented group provided a fantastic experience for our community last year, and
we are eager to continue building on that momentum as we move toward the grand
opening of our newly completed Fair Oaks Village Park and Fair Oaks Performing Arts
Center.

When we booked Take Note Troupe for their 2025 season, we anticipated that our new
performance space would be available to accommodate their needs. However, given the
current timeline for completion, we are unable to host them in our new space and our
portable stage is unfortunately not large enough for their students. To ensure that the
performance can proceed as planned, we are seeking funding assistance to rent an
appropriately sized stage for their production.

The total rental cost is $3,200, and while Take Note Troupe is contributing $1,400, we are
requesting a $1,800 contribution from the Foundation to help cover the remaining cost.
Shakespeare in the Park has been a valued cultural offering in and around the Sacramento
area and this is our chance to make them a community staple in Fair Oaks. A proper stage
will ensure a high-quality performance for the expanded arts opportunities coming with our
completed park. The hope is to have them perform in 2026 on Bandshell Stage in the
renovated park. By using the Bandshell Stage, they will not need to rent the stage that they
are renting this year. We believe this venue will provide the perfect setting for their
performances in the future.

We greatly appreciate the Foundation’s support and would be happy to discuss this request
further. Thank you for your consideration.

Best regards,
Jen Schuler
Arts & Entertainment Manager
Fair Oaks Recreation & Park District
